البحث الرابع إنه يخرج من الحد (ما ثبت بالأصول الثلاثة غير الكتاب من السنة والإجماع والقياس لعدم خطاب الله هناك والجواب أنها كاشفة عن الخطاب الإلهي فالثابت بها أي بالأصول الثلاثة (ثابت) (به أي بالخطاب الإلهي، فالحكم حقيقة هو ذلك الخطاب، فإن قلت : فعلى هذا يلزم أن لا يعد نظم القرآن خطاباً، لأنه كاشف أيضاً عن النفسي قال (وأما عدم نظم القرآن منه أي من الكاشف (مع أنه كاشف عن النفسي، فلأن الدال كأنه المدلول) فلا كاشفاً تأدباً، فإن قلت؛ فما بال الحنفية لا ينسبون الكشف إلا إلى القياس؟ قال : (وما عن الحنفية أن القياس مظهر بخلاف السنة والإجماع فمبني على أنه أصرح في الفرعية) فإنه يحتاج إلى أصل مقيس عليه حال أخذ الحكم بخلافهما، إذ لا يحتاج في أخذ الحكم منهما إلى شيء سواهما، فنسبوا إثبات الحكم إليهما، وكشف الحكم إليه فتأمل) فيه فإنه دقيق حقيق بالقبول (ثم في تسمية الكلام في الأزل خطاباً خلاف فبعضهم جعلوه خطاباً، والآخرون لا، يسمى أن يصير متعلقاته ، والحق أنه خلاف لفظي (إن فسر بما يفهم ولو بالأخرة أي ما فيه صلوح الإفهام (كان خطاباً فيه أي في الأزل، لأنه صالح فيه للإفهام فيما لا يزال (وإن فسر بما أفهم) أي وقع إفهامه (لم يكن في الأزل خطاباً، إذ لم يتحقق الإفهام فيه بل فيما لا يزال فقط، والخطاب في اللغة توجيه الكلام للإفهام، ثم أطلق على الكلام الموجه للإفهام فإن اكتفى بالصلوح للإفادة فالأزلي خطاب في الأزل، وإن أريد الإفهام الحالي فلا، وأما أخذ العلم بإفهامه في الجملة، كما قال السيد قدس سره فغير ظاهر، ولا يفهم من لفظ الخطاب، وما قال في «الحاشية» أن المعتبر في كون الكلام خطاباً أحد الأمرين: الإفهام ،بالفعل أو العلم في الحال بالإفهام في المآل، وأما المفهم بالقوة مع عدم العلم في الحال بكونه مفهماً في المآل فليس إلا خطاباً بالقوة عند الفريقين، فادعاء محض بل الكلام الذي هيىء للإفهام خطاب عند من يكتفي بالصلوح للإفهام في المآل علم أنه يفهم مآلاً أم لا نعم يشترط للعلم بأنه خطاب علم كونه مفهماً، فظهور الخطابية إنما هو بالعلم، وأما نفس الخطابية فبالتهيؤ والتوجه للإفهام ولو مآلاً فتأمل . (ويبتنى عليه أنه حكم في الأزل أو فيما لا يزال فمن قال الكلام خطاب في الأزل قال إنه حكم فيه، ومن لم يقل لا يقول به، فإن قلت كيف يتأتى أزلية الحكم مع أنه الخطاب المتعلق والتعلق حادث؟ قلت؛ المراد بالتعلق في الحد وقوع فعل المكلف من كالمفعول ونحوه، وليس هذا التعلق حادثاً بل الحادث التعلق بمعنى المكلف مشغول الذمة بالفعل وأين هذا من ذاك، كذا في «التحرير»، ولك أن تقول بعبارة أخرى : المراد بالتعلق في الحد التعلق الأعم من التعليقي والتنجيزي والحادث التنجيزي فتدبر.
The fourth investigation: That which is established by the three principles other than the Book—from the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas—is excluded from the definition due to the absence of Allah's address there. The answer is that they reveal the divine address. So what is established by them is established by the divine address. Thus the ruling in reality is that address. If you say: Accordingly, the wording of the Quran would not be considered address, because it too reveals the intrinsic speech. He said: As for the Quranic wording not being from it (i.e., from the revealer) even though it reveals the intrinsic speech, it is because the signifier is as if the signified, so it is not a revealer, out of deference. If you say: Why do Hanafis attribute revealing only to qiyas? He said: What is narrated from the Hanafis that qiyas is a manifestor (muzhir) unlike Sunnah and Ijma is based on the fact that it is more explicit in subordination. For it needs an analogized original when deriving the ruling, unlike the other two, which need nothing besides themselves for deriving the ruling. So they attributed establishing the ruling to them, and revealing the ruling to it. So reflect, for it is subtle and deserves acceptance. Then regarding calling the speech in pre-eternity an address, there is disagreement: some consider it an address, others do not. The truth is that it is a verbal dispute. If interpreted as 'what is understood, even eventually', i.e., what has the potential for understanding, then it is an address in pre-eternity, because it has the potential for understanding in the future. If interpreted as 'what has actually made understood', then it is not an address in pre-eternity, because understanding did not occur there but only in the future. The address in language is directing speech for understanding; then it was applied to the speech directed for understanding. If one is content with the potential for conveying, then the eternal is an address in pre-eternity. If actual current understanding is intended, then no. As for taking knowledge of its being understood in general, as al-Sayyid said, it is not apparent and is not understood from the word 'address'. And what was said in the gloss that what matters for speech being an address is one of two things: actual understanding or current knowledge of future understanding. As for that which potentially conveys without current knowledge of its being understood in the future, it is only a potential address by both groups. This is a mere claim. Rather, speech prepared for understanding is an address for those who are content with the potential for understanding in the future, whether one knows it will be understood in the future or not. Yes, for knowledge that it is an address, one needs knowledge of its being understood. So the manifestation of being an address is through knowledge, but the essence of being an address is through preparation and direction for understanding, even if in the future. So reflect. And upon this is based whether it is a ruling in pre-eternity or in the future. So whoever says the speech is an address in pre-eternity says it is a ruling there; whoever does not say that does not say it. If you say: How can the ruling be eternal while it is the address that is related, and relation is temporal? I say: What is meant by relation in the definition is the occurrence of the action of the responsible person as an object and the like, and this relation is not temporal; rather, what is temporal is the relation in the sense that the responsible person is obligated with the action. And how far is this from that? Similarly in al-Tahrir. And you may say in other words: What is meant by relation in the definition is the general relation, including both conditional and immediate, and what is temporal is the immediate relation. So ponder.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This is a rule passage. The author addresses the objection that the definition of hukm (address of Allah) excludes rulings derived from Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas since they are not directly from Allah. The response is that these sources are kashifah (revealers) of the divine address; the ruling established by them is ultimately the divine ruling. A subtle point arises: the Quranic wording itself is also a revealer of the intrinsic speech (kalam nafsi), yet it is not called a 'revealer' but rather considered identical in effect to the divine speech out of deference. The author then explains why Hanafis specifically call qiyas a 'muzhir' (manifestor) while Sunnah and Ijma are 'muthbit' (establishers): qiyas is more explicit in subordination, needing an analogical base, whereas Sunnah and Ijma directly establish the ruling without needing another source. The passage then delves into a verbal dispute about whether the eternal speech (kalam azali) can be called 'khitab' (address). The author clarifies that if 'khitab' is defined by the potential for understanding (even future), then it applies eternally; if defined by actual understanding, it only applies temporally. This distinction affects whether the ruling itself is considered eternal or temporal. The relation (ta'alluq) in the definition is general, including both conditional (ta'liqi) and immediate (tanjizi), and only the immediate relation is temporal. Thus the ruling's 'eternity' is preserved.

Key Terms
خطاب (khitāb): Speech directed for understanding; in usul, the divine address that constitutes hukm.
تعلق تعليقي (ta‘alluq ta‘līqī): Conditional relation; the relation of the divine address to the action that exists in God’s decree before the act occurs.
تعلق تنجيزي (ta‘alluq tanjīzī): Immediate relation; the relation that occurs when the responsible person becomes actually obligated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for considering the eternal speech as an address according to the author?
A) Actual understanding in pre-eternity
B) Potential for future understanding
C) The consensus of scholars
D) A direct Quranic verse

Key Takeaway
The definition of khitab as 'prepared for understanding' allows the eternal speech to be considered address, preserving the eternity of divine rulings.

Distinguishing Obligations: Allah vs Servant in Intention Requirements
Usul rule distinguishing sources of obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that distinguishes between obligations from Allah and obligations from the servant, and evaluate the differing rulings for intention in vowed fasts versus Ramadan.

Core Idea
The day's capacity for intention depends on the source: Allah's command restricts, the servant's vow does not.

This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahamut' explores a subtle but crucial distinction in Hanafi usul: why a specified vow (nadhr mu'ayyan) of fasting can be fulfilled with an intention of nafl, while the fast of Ramadan cannot. The key lies not in the act itself, but in the source of the obligation. Understanding this principle will sharpen your ability to analyse how obligations interact with time and intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core comparison
The passage compares two obligations: the Ramadan fast (from Allah) and the specified vowed fast (from the servant). Notice that both are obligatory, yet they have different rules for intention.
Focus on the phrase 'farqan bayna ijab Allah ta'ala wa ijab al-`abd'.
2
Understand the 'mi'yar' (standard) concept
The day is like a container (mi'yar) that can only hold one act of worship at a time. The question is: does the obligation 'fill' the container completely, or does it leave room for other descriptions?
The passage states: 'فلو كان مطلقه مرخصاً لما كان لافتراضه فائدة' – if the absolute were permissible, obligation would lose its benefit.
3
Trace the qiyas (analogy) for Ramadan
For Ramadan, the obligation from Allah fixes the description as 'fard'. The day cannot accept any other intention, because the divine command leaves no room. Any other intention would not be valid for fulfilling the obligation.
Ramadan is the asl (original case) in the qiyas.
4
Apply the qiyas to the vowed fast
For a vowed fast, the obligation comes from the servant's act of vowing. The day originally could have held a nafl or other obligation; the vow does not erase that inherent capacity. Therefore, intending nafl suffices for the vow, but intending another wajib (like qada') does not – because that would be a separate obligation conflicting with the vow.
The passage says: 'فإنما تعين بنذره وقد كان أيام العمر وقتاً لأداء واجب آخر' – the day was already a time for other wajib acts.
5
Note the exception and the dispute
The passage mentions a non-chosen narration (riwayah ghayr mukhtarah) where the vowed fast is not fulfilled by nafl intention. Also note the opposing view that equates vow and Ramadan. The commentator strongly supports the Hanafi position, calling the distinction 'fully clear'.
This step highlights the madhhab dispute and the tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثانية في الأحكام فلو كان مطلقه مرخصاً لما كان لافتراضه فائدة، بل يرتفع الصوم من البين اللهم إلا قليلاً، كالمعدوم، فافهم (وقد لا يكون المعيار (سبباً) للوجوب (كالنذر) المعين، فيتأدى بمطلق النية وبنية النفل إلا في رواية غير مختارة لأنه كان للناذر في ذلك اليوم صوم واحد، وكان له أن يصفه بصفة النفلية وغيرها ولما نذر به صار واجباً فلا يتصف بالنفلية، ولا يصح غيره حتى يتصف بالنفلية فهذا اليوم بالقياس إلى النفل كالليالي بالقياس إلى الصيام كله فتلغو النفلية وتبقى نيه الصوم في هذا اليوم ومصداقه ليس إلا المنذور فيصح، ولا يتأدى بنية واجب آخر) كالقضاء والكفارة بلا خلاف في رواية بخلاف (رمضان) فإنه يصح بكل نية (فرقاً بين إيجاب الله تعالى (وإيجاب العبد) فبإيجاب الله تعالى صار صوم رمضان بوصف الفرض فلا يتصف بصفة أخرى ولا يمكن غيره ليتصف وأما المنذور فإنما تعين بنذره وقد كان أيام العمر وقتاً لأداء واجب آخر، فبنذره لا يخرج صوم اليوم عن قبول وصف الوجوب، وإلا لزم المشروع، وهو معصية، ولا نذر بها، وأما إبطال النفلية فكان فيه مأذوناً من الشارع، فوقت النذر المعين محل لإيقاع الصوم مع وصف الكفارة مثلاً، وإن كان إيقاعه، إثماً لتفويت واجب النذر فانكشف الفرق بأتم وجه فلا تصغ إلى من يقول : لا فرق بين النذر ورمضان، لأنهما فرضان فلم يبق في الوقت مباينهما مشروعاً، فينبغي أن يتحد حكمهما
The second article on rulings: If its absolute were given concession, then there would be no benefit in making it obligatory; rather, fasting would be removed altogether except for a little, like nothing, so understand. (And sometimes the standard may not be a cause for obligation, like the specified vow, so it is fulfilled with absolute intention and with the intention of nafl, except in a non-chosen narration, because the person making the vow had one fast on that day, and he had the ability to describe it with the description of nafl or other, and when he vowed it, it became wajib, so it cannot be described as nafl, nor can another be valid such that it is described as nafl. So this day in relation to nafl is like nights in relation to all fasting: the nafl description is void, and only the intention of fasting on this day remains, and its actuality is nothing but the vowed fast, so it is valid. And it is not fulfilled by the intention of another wajib, like make-up or expiation, without disagreement in a narration, contrary to Ramadan, because it is valid with every intention as a distinction between the obligation of Allah (mighty and majestic) and the obligation of the servant. By the obligation of Allah, the fast of Ramadan is characterized by fard, so it cannot be described with another description, nor can another be possible to be described. As for the vowed fast, it is only determined by his vow, and the days of one's life are time for performing another obligatory act, so by his vow, the fast of the day does not leave the acceptance of the description of obligation, otherwise it would necessitate the prohibited, which is disobedience, and no vow is made for that. As for nullifying the nafl description, he is permitted to do so by the Lawgiver, so the time of the specified vow is a place for performing the fast with the description of expiation, for example, even if performing it is sinful due to missing the obligatory vow. Thus the distinction is fully clarified, so do not listen to one who says there is no difference between a vow and Ramadan, because both are obligatory, so no other intention remains in the time, so their ruling should be the same.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage from the second article discusses the ruling on intention for a specified vow (nadhr mu'ayyan) compared to Ramadan. The commentator explains that if the absolute fast (for the traveler) were given concession, it would defeat the purpose of obligation. Then he addresses the matn: 'And sometimes the standard may not be a cause for obligation, like the specified vow.' For a vowed fast on a specific day, the day can only accommodate one fast, but the person has the discretion to describe it as nafl or otherwise. Once he vows it, it becomes wajib, but the day still potentially accepts another description (like expiation) because the vow does not change the inherent capacity of the day — unlike Ramadan where Allah's command fixes the description as fard, leaving no room for another intention. Thus, a vowed fast is fulfilled with any intention (absolute or nafl), except in one non-chosen narration. It is not fulfilled by intending another wajib (like make-up or expiation) in a narration without disagreement, contrary to Ramadan where any intention suffices due to the ruling being from Allah. The distinction is that Allah's obligation is more restrictive than the servant's obligation.

Key Terms
النذر المعين (al-nadhr al-mu'ayyan): A vow to perform an act (like fasting) on a specific day.
المعيار (al-mi'yar): A standard or measure; in this context, the day as a container that can only accommodate one act.
إيجاب الله تعالى (ijab Allah ta'ala): Obligation directly from Allah, e.g., Ramadan fast.
إيجاب العبد (ijab al-`abd): Obligation created by the servant's act (vow).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, can a specified vow of fasting be fulfilled by intending a nafl fast?
A) Yes, always.
B) No, never.
C) Yes, except in one non-chosen narration.
D) Only if the vow is unspecified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between obligations from Allah (Ramadan) and from the servant (vow) regarding the capacity of a day to accommodate different intentions, because Allah's command fixes the description exclusively.

Hajj as Standard and Vessel: An Usul Analysis
Usul definition: analyzing Hajj's temporal nature as both a standard and a vessel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi usul concepts of miyar and zarf apply to Hajj and differentiate the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the immediacy of Hajj.

Core Idea
Hajj is both a standard (only one per year) and a vessel (lifetime allows multiple): its temporal nature depends on the jurist's view on immediate obligation.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the matn statement that Hajj has two aspects: it resembles both a standard (miyar) and a vessel (zarf). Understanding this duality requires grasping how Hanafi usul classifies temporal obligations. We will dissect the terms, follow the analogical reasoning, and see how the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad affects the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two analogies
The passage states that Hajj is similar to both a standard (miyar) and a vessel (zarf). Locate these terms and their initial justification.
2
Understand the basis for each analogy
As a standard: only one Hajj can fit in a single year. As a vessel: the entire lifetime can accommodate multiple Hajjs. Note how this parallels the examples of fasting (one per day) and Ramadan (multiple fasts in a month).
3
Recognize the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that Hajj is obligatory immediately (fawran), while Imam Muhammad holds that it is expansive over the lifetime (like zuhr prayer). Identify these two positions in the passage.
Abu Yusuf's view makes the first year the determined time; Muhammad's view makes the entire lifetime a vessel.
4
Apply the ikhtilaf to the analogy
Under Abu Yusuf, the first year becomes a standard because one cannot delay without sin. Under Muhammad, the lifetime is a vessel because any year is valid for performance.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Yusuf, delaying Hajj beyond the first year is sinful; according to Muhammad, it is not sinful until the end of life. This difference impacts fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والحج ذو شبهين) شبه (بالمعيار، و) شبه بـ (الظرف، فإنه لا يسع في عام واحد إلا واحداً) وبهذا شابه المعيار، كما إلا واجباً واحداً ولا يستغرق فعله وقته الذي هو أشهر الحج، وهذا آية الاتساع، وفيه يسع أن العام الواحد بعض من الوقت فإن وقته العمر كله فلا يصلح شبهاً بالمعيارية، وإلا فوقت الصلاة أيضاً معيار، إذ بعضه لا إلا صلاة واحدة، ثم عدم استغراق فعله تمام الوقت لا يسع لا يكفي للظرفية، بل سعة الوقت بفعل آخر مثله وليس أشهر العام الواحد كذلك، وها هنا وجه آخر للإشكال، أي لكونه ذا شبهين هو أن العام الأول لا يصلح إلا حجاً واحداً والتأخير عنه إثم فهو وقته والعام الآخر مشكوك فتعين للأداء فبهذا الوجه معيار وإن وجد أعوام أخرى فهي أيضاً صالحة لأداء الحج، فوسع الوقت الذي هو العمر حجاً آخر، وبهذا الوجه صار ظرفاً، كذا ذكره القاضي الإمام أبو زيد في الأسرار»، ولعل هذا الوجه هو مراد الإمام فخر الإسلام بقوله : ومعنى قولنا إنه مشكل أن وقته العمر ، وأشهر الحج في كل عام صالحة لأدائه أم أشهر الحج من العام الأول وقت متعين لأدائه؟ ويمكن حمل عبارة المتن عليه أيضاً، ثم هذا الوجه إنما يتم على رأي الإمام أبي يوسف رحمه الله فإنه يرى التعجيل واجباً، وأما على رأي الإمام محمد رحمه الله فنسبة العمر إليه نسبة وقت الظهر إليه فإن قلت الحج وإن كان وقته العمر لكنه يحتمل الموت قبل إدراك العام الثاني فالعام الأول يحتمل أن يكون هو العمر فيتضيق الوقت، ويحتمل أن يكون بعض العمر فيتسع قلت هذا لا يوجب وقوع التحديد من الشارع، بل مثله مثل الزكاة إذا تضيقت بقرب الموت والصلاة إذا تضيقت بالتأخير، بخلاف قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله فإن الوجوب عنده شرعاً على الفور، لاحتمال الموت، فيتضيق شرعاً، فإذا عاش ولم يحج العام الأول تضيق الثاني شرعاً، وصار هو مع العام الأول موسعاً،
(And Hajj has two aspects) an aspect (similar to a standard, and) an aspect similar to (a vessel, because it cannot accommodate more than one in a single year) and by this it is similar to a standard, as it cannot (except) one obligation, and its performance does not occupy its entire time, which is the months of Hajj, and this is a sign of spaciousness, and in it, the year is part of the time because its time is the entire lifetime, so it is not suitable to be similar to standard-ness, otherwise the time of prayer would also be a standard, since part of it cannot except one prayer. Then the non-occupancy of its performance of the entire time does not suffice for vessel-ness, rather the spaciousness of the time for another similar act, and the months of a single year are not like that. And there is another aspect to the difficulty, i.e., it having two aspects is that the first year cannot accommodate more than one Hajj, and delaying it is sinful, so it is its time, and the next year is doubtful, so it becomes determined for performance; by this aspect it is a standard. Even if there are other years, they are also suitable for performing Hajj, so the time, which is the lifetime, is spacious for another Hajj, and by this aspect it becomes a vessel. This is what the judge Imam Abu Zaid mentioned in al-Asrar. Perhaps this aspect is what Imam Fakhr al-Islam meant by his words: 'And the meaning of our statement that it is problematic: is its time the lifetime, and the months of Hajj in each year suitable for performing it? Or are the months of Hajj from the first year a determined time for performing it?' And the expression of the matn can also be interpreted accordingly. Then this aspect is only valid according to the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, because he holds that promptness is obligatory. As for the view of Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, the relation of the lifetime to it is like the relation of the time of zuhr to it. If you say: Hajj, although its time is the lifetime, but death can occur before reaching the second year, so the first year may be the entire lifetime, so the time becomes narrow, and it may be part of the lifetime, so it is spacious. I say: this does not necessitate specification by the Lawgiver, rather it is like zakat when it becomes narrow due to approaching death, and prayer when it becomes narrow due to delay, contrary to the saying of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, because according to him, obligation is immediate by law due to the possibility of death, so it becomes legally narrow. If he lives and does not perform Hajj in the first year, the second becomes legally narrow, and it (the time) becomes spacious along with the first year.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'والحج ذو شبهين' (Hajj has two aspects). The commentator explains that Hajj is similar to both a standard (miyar) and a vessel (zarf). As a standard: only one Hajj can be performed in a single year, analogous to how a day can only accommodate one fast. As a vessel: the overall time for Hajj is one's entire lifetime, so it can accommodate multiple Hajjs if performed in different years, similar to how the month of Ramadan (the vessel) accommodates multiple fasts. The commentator then presents a deeper analysis by Imam Abu Zaid al-Dabusi from al-Asrar: the first year after the obligation is determined for Hajj (like a standard) because delaying is sinful, but subsequent years are also suitable, making the lifetime spacious (like a vessel). This depends on the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, who holds that Hajj is obligatory immediately. For Imam Muhammad, the lifetime is like the time for zuhr prayer — it is spacious until death approaches, but not legally determined in segments. The commentator argues that the possibility of death does not make the first year legally determined; it is similar to zakat and prayer becoming narrow only due to external circumstances.

Key Terms
المعيار (al-mi'yar): A standard or measure; an act that fully occupies its time, allowing no other like it simultaneously.
الظرف (al-zarf): A vessel or container; an extended time that can accommodate multiple acts of the same type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Hanafi Imam's view makes Hajj similar to a standard (miyar) in the first year?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad
D) Imam Zufar

Key Takeaway
Hajj exhibits a dual temporal nature: as a standard in the first year (on Abu Yusuf's view) and as a vessel over one's lifetime (on Muhammad's view).

A Single Ability Relates to Contradictory Actions: The Hanafi Usul Rule
A rule (far') stating the Hanafi position on a single ability's relation to opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the relationship of a single qudra to contradictory actions and apply it to infer consequences for taharah and salah.

Core Idea
One ability relates to contradictory actions both absolutely and alternately – a foundational usul rule.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut establishes a key Hanafi usul principle: a single capacity (qudra) can serve as the basis for multiple mutually exclusive actions. The text contrasts the Hanafi view with that of opponents who require separate abilities for each opposite. Understanding this rule is essential for grasping the Hanafi theory of obligation (taklif) and the unity of moral capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
Recognize that the text asserts a single qudra relates to contradictory actions. This is a far' (branch) within usul al-fiqh.
2
Distinguish the two modes of relation
The text specifies that the relation is mutlaqan (absolutely, i.e., as a potential) and la ma'an (not simultaneously). It also rejects 'badalan' (alternately) in the sense of separate abilities.
The phrasing 'mutlaqan la ma'an' is key: absolute potential but not simultaneous actualization.
3
Locate the opposing view
The opponents hold that each opposite requires its own specific ability, so the ability for one opposite is different from the ability for the other.
The opponents are not named here but likely include Mu'tazila or later Ash'aris.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a single state of taharah can serve for multiple acts of worship (e.g., prayer and touching the mushaf) because the same ability relates to these contradictory (non-simultaneous) acts.
The opponents would require separate abilities, potentially leading to repeated purification.
5
Note the authority weight
The rule is stated without explicit proof (dalil). It is accepted as a foundational principle in Hanafi usul.
The text relies on the authority of the Hanafi school rather than a specific proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرع (القدرة الواحدة تتعلق بالأمور المتضادة خلافاً لهم فإنهم لا يقولون بتعلق القدرة الواحدة بالأمور المتضادة (مطلقاً لا معاً) يكون نسبتها إلى الضدين على السواء (ولا بدلاً) في زمانین، بل قدرة هذا الضد غير قدرة الضد الآخر .
Branch: A single ability relates to contradictory actions, contrary to them, for they do not hold that a single ability relates to contradictory actions (absolutely, not simultaneously) so that its relation to the two opposites is equal, (nor alternately) in two moments. Rather, the ability for one opposite is different from the ability for the other opposite.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This short branch (far') establishes a key Hanafi usul principle: a single ability (qudra) can relate to multiple contradictory actions. The opponents (likely some Mu'tazila or others) hold that a specific ability is required for each specific action, especially for opposites. The Hanafi position, as stated, is that ability relates to opposites both absolutely (in terms of capacity) and alternately (in time), meaning that the same ability can serve as the basis for either action, though not both simultaneously. The text explicitly rejects the idea that ability for one opposite is a separate entity from ability for the other. This principle has implications for fiqh: a valid wudu allows a person to pray or touch the mushaf, etc., with the same state of purity.

Key Terms
القدرة الواحدة (al-qudra al-wahida): A single instance of ability (qudra) that can relate to multiple actions.
الأمور المتضادة (al-umur al-mutadadda): Contradictory actions, such as movement and rest, or belief and disbelief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only simultaneously, not alternately.
B) Absolutely and alternately, but not simultaneously.
C) Only alternately, not absolutely.
D) Neither absolutely nor alternately.

Key Takeaway
A single qudra relates to contradictory actions both as a universal potential and through alternate actualization, forming a foundational Hanafi usul principle.

Obligation of Qada with Presumed Ability
Debate on obligation when time is tight due to presumed ability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on qada when time is too short for the full prayer and evaluate Imam Zufar's objection.

Core Idea
Presumed ability (qudra mutawahhama) suffices for the obligation of qada even when performance is impossible.

This passage delves into a subtle usul dispute: if a person reaches the last moment of prayer time with only enough time for a small part (e.g., one takbir), is he obligated to make up the prayer? The Hanafi school, relying on the concept of presumed ability, says yes, while Imam Zufar argues the time is unfit for performance. We will analyze the rational arguments and see how the chosen view (al-mukhtar) prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
First, locate the two opposing positions: the majority Hanafi view (obligation of qada) versus Imam Zufar's view (no obligation).
The dispute hinges on whether the last part of time can be a cause (sabab) for obligation when performance is ordinarily impossible.
2
Understand the Concept of Presumed Ability
Grasp the key term 'qudra mutawahhama' – presumed ability based on a plausible possibility (like the sun stopping). This is the pillar of the majority argument.
Presumed ability is not actual ability; it arises from the possibility of time extension, even if improbable.
3
Analyze the Arguments and Rebuttals
Trace the argument: the last part of time is the cause; presumed ability suffices for obligation; inability at the moment shifts to the substitute (qada). Then consider Zufar's objection and the responses.
The author compares with the sleepers (who can pray after waking) and the corrupted supererogatory prayer (where a part must be completed).
4
Evaluate the Tarjih and Its Practical Impact
Note that the text says Imam Zufar's view is 'most analogous' but the established fatwa is based on ihtiyat (precaution). Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: a person with only one takbir left must pray ada and then qada.
This shows how usul ijtihad leads to different practical rulings.

If he meant the remaining of time by an increase of parts, then what was objected to 'al-Tahrir' applies. And by this the unity of performance and qada becomes problematic. The initiator of divine secrets answered the first by saying that conjunction between the cause of the cause and the effect is not obligatory; how so? The sighting of the month is a cause for the obligation of fasting without conjunction. As for the second, it has preceded in the issue of unity of two causes that the very obligation of performance established in the liability is the obligation of qada. And we have a verification that benefits you. But there remains here a tricky statement: the leading of the cause to obligation of something in the liability, even if it is compelling, is only to what is suitable for obligation, and it has passed that the ordinarily impossible is not suitable for obligation legally, and that the benefit of obligation is the correctness of performance, and this is not possible, for time is not suitable for it ordinarily, unlike the sleeping person, for performance after sleep is ordinarily possible, as is not hidden. This, and Allah knows best His rulings. (Or) it is entailed upon the obligation of a part of the performance as in supererogatory if it is corrupted, for it is only obligated to make it up to preserve what is obligated to be preserved, which is the performed part. So here too, since the part of the obligatory that the last time accommodates by grasping it has become obligatory, making up the whole was obligated to preserve it, except that the obligation of the part there is by initiation and here before it. This also is insufficient, because the Law only commands us to pray in these times, not upon their parts independently but within the whole. So if the whole is not ordinarily possible, the condition of its obligation is missing, so performing its parts that the last time accommodates was not obligated, unlike the corrupted supererogatory for initiation is realized and what was performed was a good act, so it must be preserved by completion. This has made clear that the most similar is the statement of Imam Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, but precaution in the chosen (so reflect) and be fair.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a detailed juristic debate (jadal) about the obligation of qada (make-up prayer) when the time for prayer becomes extremely tight (al-mudiq). The core issue: if a person has only enough time to perform a small part of the prayer (e.g., one takbir) in the last moment, is he obligated to pray with the intention of ada (performance) or qada? The author argues that presumed ability (qudra mutawahhama) — based on the possibility that time might extend by stopping the sun — suffices for the obligation of qada. He cites Imam Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) and references a story of Prophet Solomon. The discussion covers various objections: the indivisible part of time, the covering of a large act (prayer) over a small time, and the difference between real and epistemological last part (al-manat al-akhir al-waqi'i vs al-'ilmi). The passage concludes that the opinion of Imam Zufar (that qada is not obligatory) is the most analogous (ashbah), but precaution is in the chosen view (al-mukhtar). The commentary is typical of later Hanafi usul works, engaging with the argument that the possibility of ability is sufficient for imposing obligation, a rational proof from necessity.

Key Terms
المناط الأخير الواقعي (al-manat al-akhir al-waqi'i): The real last part of time, as it exists in reality, regardless of human knowledge.
القدرة المتوهمة (al-qudra al-mutawahhama): Presumed ability based on a plausible possibility (here, possibility of time extension).
الجزء الأخير (al-juz' al-akhir): The final part of the prayer time, which is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Presumed ability (qudra mutawahhama) is sufficient for the obligation of qada in the Hanafi school, even when performance is impossible.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
beginner
6 min
Possible Ability Not Required for Qada
Rule that possible ability is not a condition for qada, with reasoning from unity of cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that possible ability (qudra mumkina) is not a condition for the obligation of qada by identifying the unity of cause (ittihad al-sabab) and distinguishing between the conditions for the initial obligation (ada) and its continuation.

Core Idea
The obligation of qada is a continuation, not a new obligation; thus the ability condition is not repeated.

This lesson explains a foundational Hanafi usul rule: possible ability (qudra mumkina) is not required for the obligation of make-up (qada). The reasoning hinges on the concept that the condition of ability applies only to the initial direction of obligation (tawajjuh al-taklif). Since the obligation of qada is a continuation of the original obligation — the cause (sabab) is the same — the condition already fulfilled for ada does not need to be repeated. Understanding this rule helps clarify when and why a person must make up missed acts of worship even if they currently lack full capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling (hukm)
State the Hanafi position: possible ability is not a condition for the obligation of qada. This means that when a person misses a wajib act they were able to perform at its original time, they remain obligated to make it up even if they are no longer able to perform it with the same ease.
The ruling is absolute for all wajib acts that were originally obligatory with ability.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The text gives two key reasons: (1) The condition of ability is only for the direction of obligation (tawajjuh al-taklif), i.e., to make the act initially obligatory. (2) Since the cause (sabab) for qada is the same as for the original act (e.g., the time for prayer), the obligation is a continuation, not a new one.
The phrase 'ittihad al-sabab' (unity of cause) is central to the Hanafi position.
3
Apply to a concrete scenario
Consider a person who missed Zuhr prayer because they overslept. At the time of Zuhr, they were healthy (had ability). Later, before making it up, they become severely ill. According to the rule, they are still obligated to make up Zuhr if they recover, because the original obligation was established with ability. The condition does not need to be present at the time of qada.
If the person was permanently unable from the start (e.g., minor), the original obligation never arose, so qada is not required.
4
Distinguish from other schools
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may treat qada as a new obligation, requiring ability at the time of making up. The Hanafi view emphasizes continuity. Recognize that this difference reflects a deeper usul principle about the nature of qada.
This difference can have practical effects, e.g., in cases of permanent disability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة ( لا يشترط القدرة الممكنة للقضاء) أي لوجوبها عندنا ، لأن الاشتراط) أي اشتراط القدرة للوجوب إنما هو الاتجاه التكليف لا غير وقد تحقق التكليف لإيجاب الأداء حين وجود القدرة ووجوب القضاء بقاء ذلك الوجوب لاتحاد السبب أي سبب وجوب القضاء والأداء (فإذا لم يتكرر (الوجوب في القضاء (لا يجب تكرر القدرة التي هي شرط الوجوب فإذا ليس
Issue: (Possible ability is not required for qada) i.e. for its obligation in our view, because the condition of ability for obligation is only for the direction of obligation (tawajjuh al-taklif) and nothing else. And the obligation was already realized for the performance at the time of existence of ability, and the obligation of qada is a continuation of that obligation due to the unity of the cause, i.e. the cause of the obligation of qada and performance are the same. (So if the obligation is not repeated in qada, the repetition of the ability which is the condition of the obligation is not required). So not.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a clear rule (mas'ala) from Hanafi usul: possible ability (qudra mumkina) is not a condition for the obligation of qada (make-up). The reasoning is foundational: the condition of ability for obligation (taklif) was already met at the time of the original wajib (ada). Since qada is essentially the same obligation continuing (the cause is the same), there is no need for a new ability condition. If qada were a new and separate obligation, then ability would be required anew, but it is not. This principle has practical implications: if someone becomes able to perform a missed prayer only later, he must make it up even if he currently lacks the ability (e.g., he is ill but recovers). Conversely, if someone permanently loses ability (e.g., dies), the obligation transfers to the heir as a debt? That is another mas'ala. The passage ends abruptly, but the rule is complete.

Key Terms
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): Possible ability: the general capacity to perform an act. In this context, the type of ability that is a condition for the initial obligation (ada) but not for qada.
اتحاد السبب (ittihad al-sabab): Unity of cause: the cause (sabab) for qada and ada is the same, so the obligation does not become independent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is possible ability (qudra mumkina) not required for the obligation of qada (make-up)?
A) Because qada is a new and independent obligation.
B) Because the cause (sabab) for qada is the same as for the original performance, and the condition of ability was already fulfilled.
C) Because qada is only recommended, not obligatory.
D) Because the Prophet exempted the community from ability for make-up.

Key Takeaway
Possible ability is not required for qada because the obligation is a continuation, and the condition of ability was already fulfilled for the original act.

Sinful Travel and Legal Dispensations: The Itlaq Argument
Dispute on whether sinful travel qualifies for legal dispensations like shortening prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sinful travel, explain how the itlaq of Quranic texts supports it, and evaluate the opposing qiyas arguments with the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The cause of the dispensation is travel itself, not the traveler's intention.

The Hanafi school holds that even a sinful journey – like traveling to commit robbery – still qualifies for legal concessions such as shortening prayer and breaking fast. This view is rooted in the principle of itlaq: the Quranic and prophetic texts mention 'travel' without any qualification of obedience or sin. In this lesson, we will trace the Hanafi proof, examine the counterarguments from the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools, and see how the Hanafis defend their position by distinguishing the cause from an adjacent sin.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the dispute
Recognize that the question is whether the legal dispensation (rukhsa) for travel applies when the travel itself is for a sinful purpose. The Hanafi school says yes; the other three schools say no.
This is a classic usul dispute about the scope of a cause (sabab) when a prohibited intent is present.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof: Itlaq al-nusus
Identify that the Hanafis rely on the absolute wording of Quran 2:184 and the hadith on shortening prayer, which do not restrict travel to obedient ends. According to Hanafi usul, an absolute text (mutlaq) or a general text (amm) applies to all its instances unless a specific restrictor (muqayyid) is proven.
The passage explicitly says 'al-itlaq' – the absoluteness of the texts.
3
Examine the opposing proof: Qiyas
The opponents argue that the dispensation is a blessing, and blessings are not attained by sin. They analogize sinful travel to intoxication (which does not bring ease) and also cite the verse on necessity (2:173) where the dispensation to eat carrion is restricted to non-transgressors.
Understand both analogies: (1) intoxication as a cause that is itself sin, (2) the necessity verse as a restrictor.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that sin is not the travel itself but merely adjacent to it; the cause is still travel. They reject the qiyas because the cause in the analogy (intoxication) is itself the sin, whereas travel is not sinful by nature. They also reinterpret the necessity verse to refer to overeating, not to the traveler’s intent.
This is a key distinction: sin as cause vs. sin as accompaniment.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: According to the Hanafi school, a highway robber who travels may shorten his prayer; according to the other schools, he must pray fully. This shows the real-world impact of the usul principle.
This helps connect abstract usul reasoning to fiqh outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة سفر المعصية) أي سفر يكون الغرض منه فعلاً هو معصية، كسفر البغاة وقطاع الطريق (لا يمنع الرخصة عندنا خلافاً للأئمة الثلاثة الشافعي ومالك وأحمد، فعندهم يمنع الرخصة، وأما كونه سفر طاعة فلم يعلم اشتراطه عن أحد إلا من الروافض (لنا الإطلاق) أي إطلاق النصوص عن التقييد بنفي كونه للمعصية، والمطلق يجري على إطلاقه إلا لضرورة، وليست قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فَمَن كَانَ مِنكُم مَّرِيضًا أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ ) وهو أعم من كونه للمعصية أو للطاعة ﴿فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَّ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٨٤] أي فواجب عليه عدة من أيام أخر (وفي صحيح مسلم» عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما : فرض الله الصلاة على لسان نبيكم في الحضر أربعاً وفي السفر) وهو مطلق (ركعتين) اتباع الأئمة الثلاثة (قالوا : الرخصة نعمة فلا تنال بالمعصية) فإن المعصية لا تكون موجبة وسبباً للرفاهية (كالسكر) من المحرم لا يكون سبباً لنعمة الترفيه (قلنا) مسلم أن النعمة لا تنال بالمعصية، لكن المعصية ليست إياه أي السفر (بل مجاورة له ألا ترى أنه لو نوى الطاعة انقلب ذلك السفر طاعة والسبب هنا نفس السفر لا مع كونه معصية (فصار كالصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة فإنها لما لم تكن نفسها معصية أسقطت الواجب (بخلاف السبب المعصية نفسها كالسكر بشرب المسكر المحرم فإنه لا يصلح سبباً للنعمة، ذكر أن السفر لما كان مما يبتني عليه بعض العبادات، كالجهاد والحج وغيرهما، وأكثر أمور المعاش كالتجارة ونحوها، وكان لا يخلو عن نوع مشقة في الأغلب رتب الله تعالى عليه حكماً أخف، وجعله سبباً للرخصة لهذا الخير الكثير، فلا تبطل سببيته بعروض معصية مجاورة له بتقصير من المكلف، ولا يبطل الخير بمجاورة الشر، وليس مقصود الشارع من شرع الرخصة الترفيه بالمعصية، بل بما هو في ذاته منبع الطاعة والمعاش وطلب الرزق الحلال، فلا يرد أن إناطة الشارع الرخصة بما هو يلزمه وقصد منه المعصية لا يليق وشدد وادعى أنه لا نظير له، وقالوا أيضاً : قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنِ اضْطُرَّ غَيْرَ بَاغٍ وَلَا عَادٍ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۷۳] أي في أكل الميتة خص هذه الرخصة بغير الباغي، فيعمم في غيره بالقياس قلنا : تأويله غير باغ على نفسه بالتجاوز عن الحد في الأكل ولا عاد على غيره من المضطرين بأخذ ميتتهم، على أنه لا يصح القياس فإن هذا القيد لا يوجب نفي الحكم عن غيره، بل إن أفاد ذلك فللحرمة الأصلية، فلا وجه للقياس عليه على أن الإطلاق في الرخص الأخرى مانع عن القياس فتدبر
Issue: Travel for sin – i.e., travel whose purpose is an act of sin, like the travel of rebels and highway robbers – does not prevent the license according to us, contrary to the three imams al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, for according to them it prevents the license. As for it being travel for obedience, its requirement is not known from anyone except the Rawafid. Our proof is the absolute (itlaq) of the texts, free from restriction by negation of being for sin, and the absolute runs on its absoluteness unless there is necessity, and there is none. Allah said: 'So whoever among you is ill or on a journey' – and it is more general than being for sin or obedience – 'then a number of other days' (2:184), i.e., a number of other days is obligatory. And in Sahih Muslim from Ibn Abbas: 'Allah prescribed the prayer on the tongue of your Prophet: four in residence and two in travel' – and it is absolute. The three imams followed (this). They said: The license is a blessing, so it is not attained by sin, for sin does not cause or become a reason for ease, like intoxication from the prohibited does not become a reason for the blessing of relief. We reply: We affirm that a blessing is not attained by sin, but the sin is not the travel itself; rather it is adjacent to it. Do you not see that if he intends obedience, that travel turns into obedience? The cause here is travel itself, not its being accompanied by sin. So it becomes like prayer in usurped land: since it is not itself sin, it fulfills the obligation. Unlike the cause being sin itself, like intoxication from drinking the prohibited intoxicant; it does not serve as a cause for blessing. It was mentioned that since travel is something upon which some acts of worship are built – like jihad, hajj, and others – and most livelihood matters like trade and the like, and it is not free from some hardship in most cases, Allah ordained upon it a lighter ruling and made it a cause for the license for this abundant good. So its causality is not nullified by the occurrence of a sin adjacent to it due to the mukallaf's shortcoming, and good is not nullified by the proximity of evil. The Legislator's purpose in legislating the license is not to give ease through sin, but rather through what is in itself a source of obedience, livelihood, and seeking lawful provision. So there is no ground for objections. They also said: Allah said: 'But whoever is forced, neither desiring nor transgressing, then no sin upon him' (2:173) – that is, regarding eating carrion; He specified this license for the non-desiring one, so generalize it to other things by analogy. We reply: Its interpretation is: not desiring against oneself by exceeding the limit in eating, and not transgressing against others of the needy by taking their carrion. Moreover, analogy is not valid, because this restriction does not necessitate negating the ruling for others; even if it does, it is due to original prohibition. So there is no basis for analogy, because absoluteness in other licenses prevents analogy; reflect.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute concerning the applicability of legal dispensations (rukhsa) to travel that is sinful (e.g., traveling to commit robbery). The Hanafi position, stated here, is that such travel does not prevent the dispensation – such as shortening prayer or breaking fast – because the cause (sabab) is travel itself, not the intent. The text argues from the absoluteness (itlaq) of Quranic and hadith texts that mention travel without qualification. The opponents (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) argue that a dispensation is a blessing, and blessings are not earned by sin; they analogize to intoxication which does not bring relief. The Hanafi response distinguishes between sin that is the cause itself (like drinking) and sin that is merely adjacent to the cause (like traveling for sin). The adjacent sin does not nullify the causality. The opponents also cite the verse on necessity (2:173) where the dispensation to eat carrion is restricted to non-transgressors. The Hanafis reinterpret that restriction as referring to overeating, not to the sin of being a transgressor. They further argue that the general texts on other dispensations prevent such analogy. The passage concludes with "fatadabbar" (reflect), indicating the strength of the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
الرخصة (al-rukhsa): A legal dispensation that lightens the original obligation due to a legitimate excuse like travel.
الإطلاق (al-itlaq): The state of a text being unrestricted by any condition or qualification.
سفر المعصية (safar al-ma'siya): Travel whose purpose is a sinful act, e.g., traveling to commit robbery or rebellion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof that sinful travel qualifies for legal dispensations?
A) The texts about travel are absolute and include all travel.
B) Sinful travel is exempted by ijma.
C) The dispensations are only for sinful travel.
D) The opponents agree on this point.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the cause of the travel dispensation is travel itself, not the traveler's intention; therefore sinful travel still qualifies.

The Scope of Rukhsah: Refuting Qiyas from the Verse on Compulsion
Hanafi refutation of opponents' attempt to restrict rukhsah via qiyas from the verse on compulsion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a restriction (qayd) in one text does not generalize by qiyas to other texts, and you will be able to identify the key interpretive steps used to block such qiyas.

Core Idea
A restricted rukhsah does not imply restriction on all rukhsahs.

This passage is a Hanafi defense of the broad scope of concessions (rukhsah). Opponents sought to restrict all concessions by analogizing from the verse on compulsion (2:173). The commentator provides a multi-layered response: a narrow interpretation of the key term, a logical principle that a restriction does not negate the ruling for others, and the overriding effect of unrestricted (mutlaq) texts. Understanding this argument is crucial for correctly applying the rules of rukhsah and for appreciating the Hanafi method of dealing with textual restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponents cite the verse 'whoever is compelled, without being rebellious or transgressor...' to argue that the concession for eating carrion is only for non-transgressors. They then use qiyas to claim that every concession (e.g., for trade) must also be restricted to non-transgressors.
This is a classic move: taking a restriction from one text and extending it by analogy.
2
Analyze the Hanafi linguistic response
The Hanafis interpret 'baghin' and 'adin' narrowly: 'baghin' means exceeding the limit in eating, not general transgression. Thus the restriction is specific to the act of eating carrion.
This ta'wil (interpretation) confines the restriction to its immediate context.
3
Evaluate the logical rebuttal
The commentator argues that even if the restriction seems to negate the ruling for non-transgressors, that negation is due to the original prohibition (hurmah asliyyah) of carrion, not because the concession itself is conditioned. Therefore, the restriction does not establish a general rule for all concessions.
The default is prohibition; the concession lifts it for the compelled. The restriction then clarifies who is excused from the sin, not who is eligible for the concession.
4
Apply the overarching principle of mutlaq texts
The concessions for worldly transactions (trade, etc.) are given in general (mutlaq) terms in other texts. A general text cannot be restricted by qiyas from a specific text without clear evidence. Thus, the unrestricted language blocks the qiyas.
This 'mannā' (preventer) is a key tool in Hanafi usul: al-mutlaq yajri 'alā itlāqihi.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi outcome
The result is that the concession for trade remains valid for everyone, regardless of their transgressive behavior in other matters, as long as the act itself is lawful. The sin of the individual does not nullify the inherent concession.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is a broad scope of rukhsah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعاش كالتجارة ونحوها، وكان لا يخلو عن نوع مشقة في الأغلب رتب الله تعالى عليه حكماً أخف، وجعله سبباً للرخصة لهذا الخير الكثير، فلا تبطل سببيته بعروض معصية مجاورة له بتقصير من المكلف، ولا يبطل الخير بمجاورة الشر، وليس مقصود الشارع من شرع الرخصة الترفيه بالمعصية، بل بما هو في ذاته منبع الطاعة والمعاش وطلب الرزق الحلال، فلا يرد أن إناطة الشارع الرخصة بما هو يلزمه وقصد منه المعصية لا يليق وشدد وادعى أنه لا نظير له، وقالوا أيضاً : قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنِ اضْطُرَّ غَيْرَ بَاغِ وَلَا عَادٍ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۷۳] أي في أكل الميتة خص هذه الرخصة بغير الباغي، فيعمم في غيره بالقياس قلنا : تأويله غير باغ على نفسه بالتجاوز عن الحد في الأكل ولا عاد على غيره من المضطرين بأخذ ميتتهم، على أنه لا يصح القياس فإن هذا القيد لا يوجب نفي الحكم عن غيره، بل إن أفاد ذلك فللحرمة الأصلية، فلا وجه للقياس عليه على أن الإطلاق في الرخص الأخرى مانع عن القياس فتدبر
Worldly transactions such as trade and the like are not free from some hardship in most cases, so Allah Most High has placed upon them a lighter ruling and made them a cause for concession for this great good. Thus their causal efficacy is not nullified by the occurrence of an adjacent sin due to the obligator's shortcoming, nor is good nullified by the proximity of evil. It is not the intention of the Lawgiver in legislating concession to provide ease for sin, but rather for what is in itself a source of obedience and livelihood and seeking lawful provision. Therefore, it cannot be objected that the Lawgiver attaching concession to something that entails sin and is intended as sin is not appropriate and is severe, and he claimed it has no parallel. They also said: Allah says: 'But whoever is compelled, without being rebellious or transgressor, then no sin is upon him' (Al-Baqarah 2:173) meaning regarding eating carrion: He specified this concession for the non-transgressor, so it should be generalized to others by qiyas. We say: Its interpretation is 'not rebellious against himself by exceeding the limit in eating, and not transgressor against other compelled persons by taking their carrion'. Moreover, qiyas is not valid because this restriction does not necessitate negation of the ruling for others; rather if it does indicate that, it is due to original prohibition. So there is no basis for qiyas upon it, and also the generality in other concessions prevents qiyas. So reflect.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) defending the Hanafi position on rukhsah. The author first establishes that concession for worldly transactions is based on the generality of benefit and the inherent hardship, not on the sin that may accompany them. Then he addresses an objection: opponents cite the verse on compulsion (2:173) which restricts the concession to non-transgressors, arguing by qiyas that all concessions should be similarly restricted. The Hanafi response interprets 'baghy' and 'adwān' narrowly: not exceeding in eating or taking others' share. More fundamentally, the restriction in that verse does not negate the ruling for others; if it seems to, it is due to the original prohibition of carrion, not because of the concession. Moreover, concessions in general are unrestricted (mutlaq), which prevents qiyas. The passage concludes with 'fata'ammal' urging careful thought.

Key Terms
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): A concession that allows an otherwise prohibited act due to necessity or hardship.
القيد (al-qayd): A restriction or condition attached to a ruling.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning from a known ruling to a new case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why does the restriction in verse 2:173 (about compulsion) not apply by qiyas to other concessions such as those for trade?
A) Because the verse is abrogated.
B) Because the restriction is interpreted narrowly and the concessions for worldly matters are unrestricted.
C) Because trade is not mentioned in the Quran.
D) Because the verse only applies to eating carrion.

Key Takeaway
The restriction in one rukhsah verse does not automatically apply to all concessions; each concession has its own basis and scope.

Methods of Knowing Linguistic Assignments and the Qiyas Debate
Describes methods of knowing linguistic assignments and the debate on qiyas in language.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three methods of knowing linguistic assignments (tawatur, ahad, and reason) and apply the Hanafi position that qiyas is not permissible for extending lexical meanings.

Core Idea
Linguistic assignment is known through transmission, not analogy — qiyas in language is rejected for lexical meanings.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, we explore how we know the meanings of words (al-wad'). The author presents three methods: mass transmission (tawatur), single reports (ahad), and reason aided by transmission. He then addresses a controversial question: can we use analogical reasoning (qiyas) to extend a word to a new meaning? The Hanafi school firmly rejects this for lexical assignments, allowing qiyas only for clear grammatical patterns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sources of linguistic knowledge
The passage lists tawatur (mass transmission), ahad (single reports), and reason (with transmission) as methods to know linguistic assignments. Understand each source and its epistemic value.
Tawatur yields certainty; ahad provides probable knowledge; reason is only supplementary.
2
Understand the dismissal of skepticism about tawatur
The author dismisses objections that tawatur does not produce knowledge as sophistry (safsatah), because it contradicts necessary knowledge.
3
Define qiyas in language
Qiyas in language means extending a word from its known meaning to another meaning based on a shared appropriateness (munasabah). Example: extending 'khamr' (wine) to 'nabidh' (date wine) due to intoxication.
This is distinct from legal qiyas in fiqh.
4
Analyze the Hanafi position on qiyas in language
The majority (including Hanafis) reject qiyas for lexical meanings. Only when the assigner (Allah) has established a universal rule (e.g., morphological pattern) is qiyas permissible, as in verb conjugations.
Hanafi usul holds that language is known through transmission, not reason.
5
Examine the opposing view and its rebuttal
Al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and a small group allow qiyas in language, analogizing to legal qiyas. The Hanafi response invokes circularity (dawr) and the specificity of linguistic assignments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الآن في معرفة الأوضاع (التواتر كالنور والنار والتشكيك فيه بأن التواتر غير مفيد للعلم، وأن لفظ الله أكثر دوراً مع الاختلاف فيه وأمثالهما (سفسطة) لا يلتفت إليه لكونه مخالفاً للضرورة القاطعة (و) الطريق في المعرفة (الآحاد أيضاً، كنقل الأصمعي والخليل (وقد يستمد بالعقل) في إثبات الوضع لكن مع اشتراك النقل (كقولنا : الجمع المحلى باللام ( يدخله الاستثناء) وهذه المقدمة استقرائية (وكل ما يدخله المستثنى منه لأنه أي الاستثناء لإخراج ما لولاه لوجب دخوله) وهذه مقدمة يعم الاستثناء عقلية . مسألة: (هل يجوز القياس في اللغة بأن كان الواضع وضع لفظاً معيناً لمناسبة فيحكم بوجود تلك المناسبة في غيره بأنه موضوع أيضاً كالخمر للنبيذ للتخمير) قياساً على كونه(۱) العنب المشتد (والسارق) الموضوع للآخذ خفية عن حرز (للنبَّاش) قياساً عليه (للأخذ خفية) وأما إذا ثبت من الواضع اعتبار قاعدة كلية باعتبار شمول مفهوم لمعان في وضع اللفظ فلا نزاع فيه، وأنه جائز كقياس ضرب على نصر في كونه للماضي (فجوّزه شرذمة قليلة ومنهم القاضي) أبو بكر الباقلاني (قياساً على القياس الشرعي بجامع أنه لإثبات ما للمعلوم للمسكوت، فإن قيل : هذا قياس في اللغة فإثبات القياس في اللغة بهذا القياس دور، وأجيب بأن القياس عبارة عن إثبات وضع لفظ مسكوت عنه بالقياس على معلوم الوضع وهذا قياس لإثبات صحة القياس
Now [we discuss] the method of knowing the assignments. (1) Tawatur (mass transmission) like 'nur' (light) and 'nar' (fire). And objecting to it that tawatur does not produce knowledge, and that the word 'Allah' has wider usage despite disagreement about it, and similar objections—this is sophistry, not heeded because it contradicts clearly necessary knowledge. (2) The method is also by ahad [reports], like the transmission of al-Asma'i and al-Khalil. (3) Reason may also be used in establishing assignment, but with the participation of transmission, like our saying: 'the plural with the definite article al- allows exception'—this premise is inductive. And 'everything that an excepted item is excluded from' because exception is for removing what would otherwise be included—this premise is rational. Issue: (Is qiyas permissible in language? Such that the assigner placed a particular word for a meaning due to an appropriateness, and then it is judged that that appropriateness exists in another [case] so that it [the word] is also assigned [to that other]—like [qiyas] of wine for date wine due to intoxication, by analogy on the basis of it being grape juice that ferments; and [qiyas of] 'sariq' (thief) which is a word for taking secretly from a safe place, for 'nabbash' (grave robber) by analogy upon it for the taking secretly. But if it is established from the assigner that he considered a universal rule, in view of the inclusion of a concept for meanings in the assignment of a word, then there is no dispute [on its permissibility], and it is allowed, like the analogy of 'daraba' (he beat) on 'nasara' (he helped) in being [something] for the past tense. A small handful permitted it, among them al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, on the basis of analogy to legal qiyas, because the shared ground (jami') is that it is for establishing the unknown from the known. If it is said: this is a qiyas in language, so proving qiyas in language by this qiyas is a circularity (dawr). And it was answered: qiyas is defined as establishing the assignment of an unstated word by analogy to a word with known assignment, and this [argument] is a qiyas to establish the correctness of qiyas.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage presents the methods by which linguistic assignments (wad') are known: (1) tawatur (mass transmission), (2) ahad reports, and (3) reason aided by transmission. The author dismisses skepticism about tawatur as sophistry. Then it addresses the controversial issue of whether qiyas (analogical reasoning) is permissible in language. The majority of scholars reject it, but a small group—including al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani—allows it. They analogize to legal qiyas, arguing that just as legal rulings can be extended by analogy, linguistic meanings can also be extended by analogy based on commonality of appropriateness. The example provided is extending the word 'khamr' (wine) to 'nabidh' (date wine) due to the common property of intoxication; and extending 'sariq' (thief) to 'nabbash' (grave robber) due to the common property of taking secretly. However, if the assigner (Allah) has established a universal rule (such as a morphological pattern for the past tense), then qiyas is undisputed, as in conjugating verbs. The circularity objection—that using qiyas to prove qiyas in language is circular—is rebutted by distinguishing between qiyas as a process and the meta-argument for its validity. The text ultimately sides with the majority view that qiyas in language is not permissible for extending lexical meanings, only for clear grammatical rules. This reflects the Hanafi position that language is primarily transmitted and not subject to analogical extension in establishing new word meanings.

Key Terms
القياس في اللغة (al-qiyas fi al-lugha): Extending a linguistic assignment from one meaning to another based on a shared appropriateness.
التواتر (al-tawatur): Mass transmission that yields certain knowledge of a word's meaning.
الوضع (al-wad'): The assignment of a word to a meaning by the original assigner (Allah or human convention).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is qiyas in language permissible without dispute?
A) When the target word has a similar meaning to the source word.
B) When the assigner has established a universal rule (e.g., a morphological pattern).
C) When the shared appropriateness is obvious.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that linguistic assignments are known through transmission (tawatur and ahad) and rejects qiyas for lexical meanings, allowing analogy only for clear grammatical patterns.

The Validity of Qiyas in Language: A Hanafi Critique
Dispute on whether analogy can be used to determine word meanings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects analogical extension of word meanings and identify the key difference between legal and linguistic qiyas.

Core Idea
Language is conventional; meaning cannot be extended by analogy because there is no causal link between word and meaning.

Can we extend the word 'khamr' to any intoxicating drink by analogy? This question is central to a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh about the scope of qiyas. While legal analogy is accepted, some scholars argued that linguistic analogy is also valid. The Hanafi school, however, draws a sharp distinction: legal qiyas operates on causal relationships between meanings, but language is conventional and arbitrary. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the Hanafi response, clarifying why the burden of proof for word meanings rests on transmission, not analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim and examples
First, understand what is being debated: whether a word can be extended to a new meaning by analogy due to shared appropriateness. The text gives examples: extending 'khamr' to nabidh because of intoxication, and 'sariq' to nabbash because of taking secretly.
These examples show the practical implication of the dispute.
2
Analyze the opponent's argument
The opponent (al-Baqillani) argues by analogy to legal qiyas: just as we establish unknown rulings from known ones in law, we should be able to establish unknown word meanings from known ones.
The opponent's proof is itself a qiyas (analogy) — a meta-level analogy.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is 'qiyas ma'a al-fariq' (analogy with a difference). In legal qiyas, the 'illa has a causal relation that necessitates the ruling rationally; in language, no such causal link exists between a meaning and the word itself. Otherwise, indication would be natural, not conventional.
This is the key epistemological distinction.
4
Recognize the examples of rejected linguistic analogies
The text mentions that scholars rejected extensions like 'al-adham' (blackish) to everything with blackness, and 'al-qarurah' (bottle) to everything that contains. This shows that even if appropriateness exists, the placement is not necessitated — it must be reported.
Sadr al-Shari'ah's principle: appropriateness validates but does not necessitate placement.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi ruling
The truth is 'la' (no) — linguistic qiyas is not permissible. The burden of proof for any word meaning is on transmitted evidence (naql) or other signs, not on mere appropriateness.
This ruling affects how Hanafi jurists interpret Quran and hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة بعصير (هل يجوز القياس في اللغة بأن كان الواضع وضع لفظاً معيناً لمناسبة فيحكم بوجود تلك المناسبة في غيره بأنه موضوع أيضاً كالخمر للنبيذ للتخمير) قياساً على كونه(۱) العنب المشتد (والسارق) الموضوع للآخذ خفية عن حرز (للنباش) قياساً عليه (للأخذ خفية) وأما إذا ثبت من الواضع اعتبار قاعدة كلية باعتبار شمول مفهوم لمعان في وضع اللفظ فلا نزاع فيه، وأنه جائز كقياس ضرب على نصر في كونه للماضي (فجوّزه شرذمة قليلة ومنهم القاضي) أبو بكر الباقلاني (قياساً على القياس الشرعي بجامع أنه لإثبات ما للمعلوم للمسكوت، فإن قيل : هذا قياس في اللغة فإثبات القياس في اللغة بهذا القياس دور، وأجيب بأن القياس عبارة عن إثبات وضع لفظ مسكوت عنه بالقياس على معلوم الوضع وهذا قياس لإثبات صحة القياس (۱) قوله : (قياساً على كونه) الخ كذا بالأصل ولعل الصواب قياساً عليه لكونه كعصير الخ. وحرر كتبه مصححه  ١٥٠ فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الأول اللغة، وأين هذا من ذاك؟ نعم : إنما ينتهض لو كان القياس في غير الشرعيات حجة (قلنا) قياس مع الفارق إذ ثبت هناك أي في القياس الشرعي (الحكم عقلاً، لأن المعنى يجذب المعنى إذ يجوز أن يكون علاقة العلية بين المعاني فيجذب المعنى العلة لمعلوله وهو الحكم، و (لا) يجذب المعنى اللفظ وإلا لزم الدلالة بالطبع فتفكر فالحق (لا) أي لا يجوز القياس في اللغة كيف ويحتمل التصريح منهم (بالمنع) عن القياس (فإن الخلاف إنما هو في تسمية مسكوت عنه هل يجوز بالقياس أم لا؟ وفيه احتمال المنع قائم، ولم يثبت هذا الجواز عموماً في الأحكام الشرعية، حتى لا يصح القياس فيها أيضاً ألا يرى أنهم منعوا طرد الأدهم) في كل ما وجد فيه دهمة (والقارورة) في كل ما فيه قرار ( والأجدل) في كل ما فيه قوة (وغيرهما مما لا يخفى) قال صدر الشريعة : اعتبار المناسبة أمر مصحح للوضع لا موجب، وليس أن كل ما يجوز يقع، فلا بد من دليل يقوم على وقوع الوضع من النقل وغيره وضاع القياس فافهم .
Issue: Is analogy permissible in language? That is, if the originator (al-wadi') placed a specific word for a certain appropriateness, then one judges that the same appropriateness exists in another thing and thus the word is also [applied] to it, such as [the word] 'khamr' (wine) for [the drink made from] raisins (nabidh) because of intoxication, by analogy on it being [the juice of] grapes that ferments. And [the word] 'sariq' (thief) placed for one who takes secretly from a secure place, [applied] to 'nabbash' (grave robber) by analogy on him [the thief] for taking secretly. But if it is established from the originator that a universal rule is considered, by virtue of the concept encompassing meanings in the placement of the word, then there is no dispute about it, and it is permissible, like the analogy of 'daraba' on 'nasara' in being past tense. So a small group permitted it, including al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, by analogy on legal analogy (qiyas shar'i) with the common factor that it establishes for the unknown what is known. If it is said: This is analogy in language, so proving analogy in language by this analogy is circular. And it was answered that analogy is the establishment of a word for an unmentioned thing by analogy on a known placement, and this [the proof] is an analogy to establish the validity of analogy in language. And what has this to do with that? Indeed, it would be valid if analogy was a proof in non-legal matters. We say: It is an analogy with a difference, because there (in legal analogy) the ruling is established rationally, because meaning attracts meaning—since it is possible that there is a causal relation between meanings, so the 'illa (cause) attracts its effect (the ruling). But [meaning does] not attract the word, otherwise it would imply natural indication. So reflect. The truth is: No, analogy in language is not permissible. How [can it be], when it is possible that they have explicitly prohibited analogy? For the dispute is only about naming an unmentioned thing—is it permissible by analogy or not? And the possibility of prohibition remains, and this permissibility has not been established generally, even in legal rulings, so that analogy would not be valid there either. Do you not see that they prohibited [extension of] 'al-adham' (the blackish one) to everything having 'duhma' (blackness), and 'al-qarurah' (bottle) to everything having 'qarar' (containment), and 'al-ajdal' (the strong) to everything having 'quwwa' (strength), and other such examples? Sadr al-Shari'ah said: Consideration of appropriateness is a factor that validates a placement, not a necessitator; and not everything that is permissible actually occurs. So there must be evidence indicating the occurrence of the placement from transmission or other means, and analogy is lost. So understand.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute over whether qiyas (analogy) can be used to extend a word from its original meaning to a new meaning based on a shared attribute (like calling nabidh 'khamr' because of intoxication). The Hanafi position, following the text, is that it is not permissible. The author mentions that a small group, including al-Baqillani, permitted it by analogy to legal qiyas. However, the reply is that legal qiyas is valid because meanings have causal relationships (the 'illa necessitates the ruling rationally), but language does not have such necessary connections—otherwise the relationship between word and meaning would be natural, not conventional. The text also warns that even if some analogical extensions were allowed, they are not generally accepted; the burden of proof for any word meaning remains on transmitted evidence or rational necessity, not mere analogy. Sadr al-Shari'ah concludes that appropriateness is a reason for valid placement, but does not necessitate it; thus one must have direct evidence of the word being used for the new meaning.

Key Terms
القياس (qiyas): Extending a word from its known meaning to a new meaning based on a shared attribute (appropriateness).
المناسبة (al-munasaba): Appropriateness or the quality that makes a word suitable for a meaning; it is a factor that validates placement (wad') but does not necessitate it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason analogy in language is not valid?
A) It leads to circular reasoning
B) Language is conventional and not based on causal relations between meanings
C) It is prohibited explicitly by the founders of language
D) It would make all words ambiguous

Key Takeaway
Language is conventional; appropriateness can validate a placement but cannot necessitate it; only transmitted evidence establishes actual word meanings.
