Is Dalaalat al-Nass Qiyas? The Hanafi Position
Debate on whether dalaalat al-nass is qiyas or linguistic indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis distinguish dalaalat al-nass from qiyas, and identify the role of al-manat as a condition for linguistic inclusion.

Core Idea
Dalaalat al-nass is linguistic indication, not qiyas; the manat is a condition for inclusion, not a cause.

A fundamental question in usul al-fiqh: When a text's ruling applies to a case because of a shared attribute, is that analogy (qiyas) or direct linguistic indication (dalaalat al-nass)? The Hanafi school insists it is the latter. This lesson unpacks the nuanced debate between Hanafis and al-Razi, clarifying how the role of the attribute (manat) as a mere condition for inclusion—not a cause—preserves the linguistic nature of the indication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What does Imam al-Razi claim about any ruling based on a necessitating meaning (al-ma'na al-mujib)? He says it is qiyas. The Hanafis disagree.
This is the starting point: the nature of the text's indication.
2
Understand the Hanafi concept of dalaalat al-nass
Hanafis define dalaalat al-nass as a linguistic indication where the text itself – through its composition – covers all instances that contain a certain attribute. The attribute is not the cause (illa) but a condition for the text's application.
Compare with qiyas: in qiyas, the ruling is extended by reason; in dalaalat al-nass, it is directly from the language.
3
Analyze the role of al-manat (the attribute)
In dalaalat al-nass, the attribute (manat) acts as a title (unwan). The text is set up to include whatever has that title. The ruling does not require a separate analogy; it is already linguistically included.
The attribute is necessary for inclusion but does not establish the ruling independently.
4
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal to al-Razi
Hanafis argue that observing the necessitating meaning does not make the ruling theoretical (nazari). It can be necessary (daruri) as in cases where the analogy is inherent (qadaya qiyasatuha ma'aha). Moreover, the meaning is only a condition for inclusion, not a cause that establishes a new ruling.
The rebuttal preserves that the indication is linguistic, not rational.
5
Apply the distinction: the benefit (thamarah)
The practical benefit appears in rulings where deniers of qiyas (like Dawud al-Zahiri) accept dalaalat al-nass but would reject the same ruling if it were considered qiyas. Thus, the classification matters for acceptance by all schools.
The Hanafi view allows broader acceptance of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية
أكثر منه ، مع أن الذرة جزء منه وداخل فيه فلا يكون قياساً، لأن اختلاف اللوازم يستلزم اختلاف الملزومات وفي المقدمة الأولى مناقشة بأن وجوب عدم اندراج الأصل في الفرع ممنوع، وإنما الممتنع الاندراج الذي يوجب الفردية، وليس الذرة فرداً من المال الكثير (كذا في شرح المختصر لكن هذا المنع إنما يتوجه لو منع ثبوت الإجماع، فإنه بعد ثبوته لا يقبل المجمع عليه المنع أصلاً، فإن قلت: لا يصح منع ثبوت الإجماع فإن النقلة ثقات، قلت : ما نقلوه إنما هو عدم الاندراج اندراج الجزئي تحت الكلي بحيث يكون الفرع متناولاً إياه لعمومه (أقول) ليس المناقشة في المقدمة الأولى فقط بل في المقدمة الثانية أيضاً من أن الأصل ههنا داخل في الفرع (لأن الأصل هو الأقل بشرط (لا أي بشرط عدم الزيادة عليه وهو ليس جزءاً من الأكثر، إنما الجزء الأقل لا بشرط الزيادة فتدبر) وأجاب عنه في التلويح بأن هذا الذي بكونه بشرط لا وإن لم يكن داخلاً فيه حقيقة، لكنه داخل لا بشرط الزيادة، وهذا ممتنع في القياس بالإجماع، وبالجملة : إن دخول الأصل في الفرع في بادىء الرأي ممتنع في القياس إجماعاً بخلاف الدلالة فافهم الإمام الرازي وأتباعه قالوا: لولا المعنى الموجب وجوده) أي وجود حكم الأصل في الفرع لما حكم فيه، فثبوت الحكم فيه لأجل المعنى الموجب وهو القياس (أقول) في الجواب ملاحظة المعنى الموجب لثبوت الحكم (لا يوجب النظرية حتى يكون قياساً كما في القضايا التي قياساتها معها فإنها ضرورية، مع أن القياس الموجب للحكم موجود هناك، وهذا غير وافٍ، إذ النظرية غير لازمة للقياس كيف وهو يقول إنه قياس جلي فافهم وأجيب في المختصر أن المعنى شرط لتناوله أي تناول الكلام لحكم المسكوت (لغة) فإن اللغة قد وضعت التركيب لتناول الحكم لما يوجد فيه المناط فملاحظة المناط إنما هي ليعلم تناول الكلام لا أنه مثبت للحكم حتى يكون قياساً، وتفصيله أن القياس يظهر في الفرع لوجود ما يقتضيه فيه لا لأن الكلام دال عليه لغة وعرفاً وأما دلالة النص فعند الجماهير دلالة لغوية للمركب والمناط شرط لتناول الحكم، وهو بمنزلة العنوان، ومن ظنها قياساً أن يزعم لا دلالة له عليه لغة ولا عرفاً، وإنما يلزم الحكم بوجود العلة غاية ما في الباب أن التعليل ووجود العلة ضروريان فصارت قياساً جلياً، فقد ظهر أن النزاع معنوي تظهر فائدته في بعض الأحكام، وإذا عرفت هذا فنقول : المعنى الموجب لا يوجب الحكم في الفرع أصلاً، وإنما يلاحظ لكونه بمنزلة العنوان، فلا يثبت مدعاكم إلا إذا ثبت أن الحكم هناك لأجل هذا المعنى ودونه خرط القتاد وهو ممنوع وبهذا القدر تم الجواب، لكن لزيادة التوضيح قال : (ومن ثم) أي من أجل أن المعنى ليس مثبتاً للحكم بل شرط للتناول اللغوي قال به النافي للقياس) كداود الظاهري وغيره وعلى ما قررنا لا يتوجه إليه قوله (وقد يقال : إن القياس الجلي لم ينكر ) فقبول المنكر له الدلالة لا يلزم منه أنها غير القياس، وأما عدم التوجه فلأنه لا يزيد على الكلام على السند فافهم
The third article on linguistic principles. More than it, while the atom is part of it and included in it, so it is not qiyas, because difference of necessary implications necessitates difference of the things necessitated. In the first premise there is a discussion: the necessity of the origin not being included in the branch is denied; what is prevented is the inclusion that causes individuality, and the atom is not an individual of much wealth. (As in Sharh al-Mukhtasar, but this denial is only valid if one denies the establishment of consensus, for once it is established, consensus cannot be denied at all. If you say: the denial of consensus is not valid because the transmitters are reliable, I say: what they transmitted is only the non-inclusion of the partial under the universal such that the branch encompasses it due to its generality. I say: the discussion is not only in the first premise but also in the second premise that the origin here is included in the branch (because the origin is the lesser with the condition of 'not' i.e. with the condition of no increase upon it, and it is not part of the greater; only the part is the lesser without the condition of increase, so reflect). And in al-Talwih the answer was given that this which is with the condition of 'not' even if it is not included in it in reality, but it is included without the condition of increase, and this is prevented in qiyas by consensus. In summary: the inclusion of the origin in the branch in the initial view is prevented in qiyas by consensus, contrary to indication. Understand. Imam al-Razi and his followers said: Were it not for the meaning that necessitates its existence (i.e. the existence of the origin's ruling in the branch), nothing would be judged in it, so the establishment of the ruling in it is because of the necessitating meaning, which is qiyas. I say: in the answer, observing the necessitating meaning for the establishment of the ruling does not necessitate theoretical knowledge such that it would be qiyas, as in matters whose qiyas are with them, for they are necessary, even though the qiyas that necessitates the ruling exists there. And this is insufficient, for theoretical knowledge is not necessary for qiyas—how can it be when he says it is clear qiyas? Understand. And in al-Mukhtasar it was answered that the meaning is a condition for its inclusion, i.e. the inclusion of the speech for the ruling of the unmentioned (linguistically), for language indeed placed the composition for the inclusion of the ruling for that in which the attribute is found; so observing the attribute is only to know the inclusion of the speech, not that it establishes the ruling as qiyas. Its detail: qiyas appears in the branch because of the existence of what necessitates it in it, not because the speech indicates it linguistically and customarily. As for indication of the text, according to the majority it is a linguistic indication of the composite, and the attribute is a condition for the inclusion of the ruling, and it is in the position of a title. And whoever thinks it is qiyas claims that there is no indication for it linguistically or customarily, and the ruling is only necessitated by the existence of the cause; the utmost is that the legal cause and the existence of the cause are necessary, so it became clear qiyas. So it has become clear that the dispute is conceptual, its benefit appearing in some rulings. And when you know this, we say: the necessitating meaning does not necessitate the ruling in the branch at all; rather it is observed as being in the position of a title, so your claim is not established unless it is established that the ruling there is because of this meaning, and without it it is a difficult task, and it is denied. With this the answer is complete. But for further clarification, he said: (Because of that) i.e. because the meaning does not establish the ruling but is a condition for linguistic inclusion, the denier of qiyas (like Dawud al-Zahiri and others) said it. And based on what we have established, his statement (It may be said: clear qiyas was not denied) does not apply to him; acceptance by the denier of indication does not necessitate that it is not qiyas. As for the non-application, it is because he does not go beyond speech on the chain. Understand.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the nature of qiyas (analogy) versus dalaalat al-nass (linguistic indication of the text). The author explains the Hanafi position that when the meaning (ma'na) that necessitates a ruling is observed in the branch (far'), it does not constitute qiyas if the text itself linguistically indicates the ruling for any instance containing that meaning. The text's inclusion of the ruling is based on the language itself, and the meaning (al-manat) is merely a condition for that inclusion, akin to a title. Therefore, the deniers of qiyas (like Dawud al-Zahiri) can accept such rulings without admitting qiyas, because it is linguistic indication. The dispute is conceptual (ma'nawi) and affects only some rulings. The passage also critiques the argument of Imam al-Razi and his followers who claimed that any ruling based on a meaning is qiyas, rebutting that the presence of a necessitating meaning does not make it qiyas if the text's language already covers the branch. The conclusion is that clear qiyas (qiyas jali) is not denied by those who accept linguistic indication.

Key Terms
القياس الجلي (al-qiyās al-jalī): A clear analogy where the cause (illa) is evident and the ruling in the branch is necessitated by the same cause as the origin
الدلالة (al-dalāla): Linguistic indication of the text, which includes the meaning (ma'na) as a condition for inclusion
المعنى الموجب (al-ma'nā al-mūjib): The meaning that necessitates the existence of the ruling; in this context, it is not the cause of the ruling but a condition for the text's inclusion
المناط (al-manāṭ): The relevant attribute that is the basis for the ruling, considered a condition (shart) for the text's inclusion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi perspective in this passage, what is the role of the meaning (al-ma'na) in dalaalat al-nass?
A) It is the cause (illa) that necessitates a qiyas ruling.
B) It is a condition (shart) for the text's linguistic inclusion of the ruling, not qiyas.
C) It is irrelevant to legal reasoning.
D) It makes the ruling theoretical (nazari).

Key Takeaway
Dalaalat al-nass is linguistic indication, not qiyas, because the attribute (manat) is a condition for the text's inclusion of the ruling, not a cause for extension.
